Jamison Brereton

38 (272)
Indra
Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra G─Бthina or Praj─Бpati Vai┼Ыv─Бmitra or Praj─Бpati V─Бcya
10 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
A dense and difficult, but rewarding, hymn. Although the hymn is found in the midst of the Maс╣Зс╕Нala III Indra hymns and is assigned to Indra by the Anukramaс╣З─л, the name Indra is not found in the hymn (save in the appended Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra refrain), and indeed it is not at all clear that there are any references to Indra in the hymn. Not surprisingly the hymn has given rise to much discussion.
Any interpretation of its contents and intent will necessarily be speculative, and the richness and multivalence of the images should not be reduced to a single and simple paraphrase. Nonetheless, we will attempt a sketch here. It is regularly remarked that the hymn is cosmogonic. In fact, it seems to concern two creations: the Ur-creation of undifferentiated material and the subsequent establishment of indi
vidual name and form. As usual in ancient India, creation is conceived of as an act of division and individuation, rather than of assemblage. This second, and more interesting, creation was carried out by the equivalent of poets, and the current poet of this hymn identifies himself and his activities with the authors of this second creation and seeks their model for his own poetic work. The large number of neu
ter pronouns of unclear reference throughout the hymn seem to be a grammatical reflection of the undifferentiated material of the first creation, and the poet seems almost to be inviting us to participate in the second creation by ourselves assigning them name and form.
The poem begins with three verses in the poetтАЩs own voice, concerning the older generations of poets and the poetic tradition. In verse 1 he sounds both tremulous and self-assured, mindful of the tradition he belongs to but also proud of his own insight. In the second verse, addressing himself (as so often) in the 2nd person, he exhorts himself to seek models from the earlier poets, and introduces the notion that they тАЬcrafted heaven for themselves,тАЭ a reference to the second creation. The third verse fleshes out this statement, in describing just how the older poets set about this creation. Most important is the final p─Бda, in which they тАЬput apartтАЭ the two worldsтАФthe primal act of separation that makes life possible.
Verse 4 moves abruptly to a new subject, or rather to an older one. A previously unmentioned figure is introduced obliquely, and though he is explicitly credited

with a тАЬnameтАЭ in p─Бda c, it is not at all clear what that name isтАФpossibly Vi┼Ыvar┼лpa тАЬpossessing all formsтАЭ of p─Бda d. In verse 5 it appears that this bull is responsible for the Ur-creation preceding the separation just described. The lack of differentia tion in the Ur-creation may be signaled by the androgyny of its sourceтАФтАЬthe bull gave birth.тАЭ The same verse also introduces two unnamed kings, тАЬsons/descendants of heaven.тАЭ This epithet in the dual usually refers to the A┼Ыvins, but this identifica tion seems unlikely here. Other suggested pairs are Mitra and Varuс╣Зa (Grassmann, Geldner) or Indra and Varuс╣Зa (S─Бyaс╣Зa, Renou, Oberlies); either pairing is perhaps possible, but the fact that the poet forebears to name them suggests that a precise identification may run counter to the poetтАЩs intentions. It might also be noted that the only identifiable dual entities in the hymn are the two world-halves (vss. 3, 8, probably 9), and in verse 8 they тАЬset all in motion.тАЭ It therefore seems possible that in this hymn the тАЬtwo descendants of heavenтАЭ could in fact be the two worlds, which have dominion over (vs. 5) and tend to (vs. 6) the тАЬ(cosmic) division,тАЭ both as products of the primal separation in the second creation and producers of the further individuation occurring in that second creation: note the increasing num
bers in verse 6ab.
In verse 7a we return to the androgynous Ur-creator, now explicitly identified as both bull and cow; the rest of the verse introduces the second creation characterized by тАЬnamesтАЭ and тАЬform.тАЭ The creators here are тАЬmasters of artifice,тАЭ poets perhaps. Verse 8 essentially repeats verse 7, as is signaled by the identical opening phrase, but this time it is the current poet himself (who made a brief reappearance in vs. 6cd), who by his praise hymn is responsible for movement in the world (i.e., the second creation) contrasted to the static golden emblem (8b) arising from the first creation. The poet thus implicitly identifies himself with the masters of artifice, the poets, in verse 7. In the final verse (aside from the refrain) both the unnamed dual pairing, quite possibly the two worlds, and the masters of artifice return to bear witness to the creative actions of the poet himself, who through his powerful tongue seems to control the individuated forms. We have thus returned to the issues raised in verse 1, but with the poet having successfully assumed his vocation and commanded the respect of his predecessors in the creative act.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra In addition to the usual tr., it is worth consulting RenouтАЩs alternative tr. in his Hymnes sp├йculatifs (29-31 + nn.), in addition to his later one in EVP XVII.

My interpr. both in detail and in overall outline differs significantly from others, but it is internally consistent and attempts to fit the many puzzling details into an overall schema. That this sometimes requires making interpretive leaps is a price IтАЩm willing to pay. I lay out and support my choices in the comments on individual vss., though I do not chart every deviation from the various other tr. and defend them against those tr.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRepeat (to Indra) pious praise, as a carpenter (plural nes the wood), and engaging (zealously in sacred rites), as a quick horse bearing well his burden; endowed with intelligence, and refllecting upon the future acts acceptable (to Indra), I desire to behold the sages (whohave gone to heaven).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As a quick horse: the instrumental tutor of the rite is supposed here to address the officiating priests, urging them to be diligent laboureres, like the carpenter of the pack-horse; acts acceptable to Indra: abhipriy─Бс╣Зi marmс╣Ы┼Ыat par─Бс╣Зi kav─лс╣Зicch─Бmi sandс╣Ы┼Ыe: priy─Бс╣Зi = indrasya priyatam─Бni;

Par─Бс╣Зi = uttam─Бni, best and most dear to Indra;

Karm─Бс╣Зi = acts; or, par─Бс╣Зi = acts to be done on subsequent days, uttare┼Ыvahassu kriyam─Бс╣З─Бni;

Kavi = kr─Бntadar┼Ы─л a seer of the past;here, it is said to mean a holy person n who, for his assiduous devotion, has attained deification, yaс╕е p┼лrvam anuс╣гс╣нhitayaj├▒aiс╕е devabh┼лyam agamat; so, ye vai tena с╣Ыс╣гayaс╕е purve pret─Бs te vai kavayaс╕е (Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 6.20)

Jamison Brereton

Like a craftsman I ponder my inspiration. Bending like a prizewinning steed amenable to the chariot-pole,
touching now on my own dear things, now on distant ones, I seek sage poets to see (these) wholeтАФ(though) I (too) have wisdom.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The 1st sg. pf. d─лdhay─Б is taken by all as a straight indicative; the Pp. reads d─лdhaya with short final vowel. My tr. тАЬI ponderтАЭ reflects this analysis (K├╝mmel [257-60] having demonstrated that the indic. pf. of this root is always presential). However, I now wonder if this form could be a subjunctive with the unextended 1st sg. subj.

ending -─Б. Although lengthened forms of the indic. pf. ending -a do exist (e.g., v├йd─Б 9x), they are relatively uncommon. And a subjunctive тАЬI shall ponder тАжтАЭ would open this speculative hymn nicely.

The standard tr. take priy─Б╠Бс╣Зi тАж p├бr─Бс╣Зi as coreferential (e.g., Oldenberg тАЬdie fernsten, lieben (Dinge, Ereignisse)тАЭ). I prefer to take the two as contrastive, the nearby familiar things dear to the poet and far-away matters almost beyond his ken – with the intensive (i.e., frequentative) part. m├бrmс╣Ы┼Ыat conveying the restless activity of his mind. Realizing that he needs the steadying hand of poetic tradition to help control his racing but fertile thoughts, in d he expresses his desire for poets belonging to that tradition to give a full account of what he is seeing – though he does not deny that he himself has wisdom.

Griffith

HASTING like some strong courser good at drawing, a thought have I imagined like a workman.
Pondering what is dearest and most noble, I long to see the sages full of wisdom.

Geldner

Wie der Zimmermann sein Werk, so habe ich das Gedicht ├╝berlegt, wie ein preisgewinnender Renner, der gut eingefahren ist, einen Anlauf nehmend. An die vertrauten fernen Dinge im Geiste r├╝hrend w├╝nsche ich, der Weise, da├Я die Seher zuschauen.

Grassmann

Wie ein K├╝nstler habe ich das Lied ersonnen, wie ein schnelles Ross, das an starker Deichsel geht, erw├дgend, was das liebste und vorz├╝glichste sei, w├╝nsche ich einsichtsvoll die Weisen zu sehen [um sie zu befragen].

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAsk of the lords (of earth, the holy teachers), the birth of those deified sages, who with well-governed minds, and diligent in sacred rites, fabricated the heavens; and may these propitiatory (praises), augmenting (your power) and rapid as the wind, reach you at this solemn rite.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Ask also the powerful generations of the poets: they as good workers, holding their minds firm, crafted heaven for themselves.
These are the precedents for you, which keep growing stronger.
Sought by mind they have now come (to rest) on its [=mindтАЩs] firm
foundation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As I see the movement of the verse, in p─Бda a the poet sets himself to question the older generations of poets about their creative activity. P─Бda b concerns this activity in the past and identifies m├бnas- тАШmindтАЩ as the foundation (тИЪdhс╣Ы) for the creative act. (I might now alter the tr. to make this clearer, to тАЬmaking their minds the foundation.тАЭ) In cd we turn to the present time and to the poet (te) (who addressed himself in a); the praс╣З─л╠А- in c (on which see further below) are the products or models derived from the creative activity in b. In d it is made clear that these precedents, actively sought by the current poetтАЩs mind, rest on the dh├бrman- тАШfoundationтАЩ not only of the mental activity of the former poets but also of his own mind.

The first technical issue in this vs. is whether pс╣Ыcha + ACC. here means тАЬask XтАЭ or тАЬask about XтАЭ (in German terms тАЬfragenтАЭ vs. тАЬfragen nachтАЭ); both uses of the accusative are possible with тИЪpс╣Ыch. Related to this question is what j├бnim─Б means in this context: тАШbirthsтАЩ, тАШgenerationsтАЩ, тАШracesтАЩ? With Geldner and Klein (DGRV I.453-54), I take j├бnim─Б kav─лn─Б╠Бm to be the personages addressed, not (with Oldenberg, Renou, Hoffmann [Inj. 225], Scarlatta [276, 288], Witzel Got┼Н) the topic of the question. The poet is widening his range of interlocutors from the current poets (1d) to the long series of generations, back to the poets who themselves participated in the creation (2b).

With all modern tr./comm, I take takс╣гata as a med. 3rd pl. middle to the athematic present to тИЪtakс╣г, rather than a 2nd pl. act. of the thematic stem, as Grassmann classifies it. I have added the self-beneficial тАЬfor themselvesтАЭ to the tr. because, though the root тИЪtakс╣г is abundantly attested, this appears to be the only middle form in the RV. In keeping with my larger interpr. of the hymn as concerning two creations, the second of which was the product of poets conjuring up the differentiated cosmos by their verbal powers, I think the medial takс╣гata here signals the intimate engagement of the poets in the act of creation and the interpenetration of the things created and the creators themselves. Note also that our current poet lays some claim to this primal act by calling himself in 1a a t├бс╣гс╣нar- тАШcraftsman, fashionerтАЩ, the agent noun to the root тИЪtakс╣г, which supplies the verb of creation in 2b.

The root-noun cmpd. praс╣З─л╠Б- is found only here in the RV, but the lexeme pr├б тИЪn─л, lit. тАШlead forthтАЩ, is very common as a verb form and in other cmpds. The word here has received a not particularly instructive variety of renderings, which I will not repeat. I think it means тАШprecedentтАЩ – that is, the work of creation engaged in by the kavis of old provides the model for the current poet. This seems a reasonable semantic extension of тАШleading forthтАЩ. The precedents keep тАЬgrowing stronger / increasingтАЭ both because the elements of creation keep proliferating and because the current poet becomes more familiar with them and adept at employing them.

In the last p─Бda these precedents that the poet has sought with his mind take up their position in his mind, ready to serve for his own creative endeavors. The older generations of poets were called тАЬfirm in mind, holding their minds firmтАЭ (or, see above, тАЬmaking their minds the foundationтАЭ)(manodhс╣Ы╠Бt-) in b; it is fitting that their models, which he тАЬsought with his mindтАЭ (m├бnov─Бta-), should now in turn take up their position on his own mindтАЩs support (dh├бrmaс╣Зi). On the basis of the cmpd.

manodhс╣Ы╠Бt- in b I supply тАШmindтАЩ as the possessor of dh├бrman-. Most tr. (Geldner, Renou [twice], Hoffmann [Inj. 225], Klein DGRV I.453-54) interpr. the loc. dh├бrmaс╣Зi as a rather vague adverbial (Geldner, Hoffmann тАЬin rechter Weise,тАЭ sim. Klein). I think it needs to be interpr. in full locatival sense; Scarlatta (276) and Witzel Got┼Н in separate ways do give it a locatival interpr. but their tr. do not reflect its connection with manodhс╣Ы╠Бt- in b.

Griffith

Ask of the sages’ mighty generations firm-minded and devout they framed the heaven.
These are thy heart-sought strengthening directions, and they have come to be sky’s upholders.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬComprehending hidden (mysteries) here on earth, they have, through their power, made manifest (the things of) heaven and earth; they have set limits to themby their elements; they connected them both mutually united, wide-spread and vast, and fixed the intermediate (firmament) to sustain them.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

They have set limits: sam m─Бtr─Бbhir mamire = m─Бtr─Бbhiс╕е rodasyau iyattay─Б paricchinne cakruс╕е, wiс╕е the elements they made determinate divisions of heaven and earth by so much, i.e., to a definite limit or extent

Jamison Brereton

And, in depositing their own secret (tracks/names) in safety just here, they ornamented the two world-halves for their dominion. (When) they fully measured (them) with their measures, they held fast the two broad (worlds). They have put apart the two great ones,
which were fitted together, to give (us) nourishment.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Before addressing the question of what p─Бdas a and b have to do with each other thematically, we must first consider the small technical issue of the placement of ut├б at the beginning of p─Бda b. Since p─Бda a contains a participle (d├бdh─Бn─Бс╕е) and p─Бda b a main verb (s├бm a├▒jan), it is unlikely that ut├б is conjoining the two p─Бdas.

Instead, with Klein (DGRV I.396-97), I think it is probably conjoining this hemistich with the preceding vs., with ut├б displaced to the beginning of p─Бda b after the participial phrase in a. This is very reminiscent of III.31.21, in this same Indra series, where the same explanation accounts for a rightward displacment of ca into the beginning of the second p─Бda of the clause.

As indicated in the published introduction, I think this vs. describes the role of the poets in the second creation. It fleshes out the laconic takс╣гata dy─Б╠Бm тАЬThey crafted heavenтАЭ in 2b. But what are they depositing in p─Бda a, and why? The first question can be restated as – what should be supplied with g├║hy─Б? The most common nouns appearing with that adjective are n─Б╠Бman- тАШnameтАЩ and pad├б- тАШtraces, trackтАЩ; either of these could work here because both can be used of the esoteric verbal production of the poets. тАЬSecret namesтАЭ would refer to the act of creation that involves dividing and naming the inchoate mass of material pre-creation; тАЬsecret tracesтАЭ would refer to the esoteric poetry more generally. Here they seem to have pooled and deployed these secret elements, to use in their poetic ornamentation – that is, in their detailed elaboration – of the originally undifferentiated matter of the two worlds. Note that the participle is middle: it is their own names/traces that are in play.

In both Hymnes sp├йc. (1956) and EVP XVII (1969) Renou tr. s├бm a├▒jan as тАЬont consacr├й,тАЭ as an allusion to royal unction. The dat. kс╣гatr─Б╠Бya тАШfor dominionтАЩ makes this a tempting idea, though s├бm тИЪa├▒j is not a standard technical term in the royal consecration. I certainly think this is a secondary meaning of this p─Бda, but in keeping with the rest of the hymn, I think the primary meaning must be creation through poetic elaboration. Since royal consecration does in fact make the person in question a new entity, the king, it can be conceptualized as a creation as well.

The 2nd half-verse is more clearly concerned with creation. The root тИЪm─Б тАШmeasureтАЩ is of course regularly used in this connection, and as I said in the published

introduction, the separation of the two worlds in d is a standard cosmogonic image. GeldnerтАЩs interpr. of c is rather aberrant and in part dependent on a passage in the PB, and his interpr. has not become the standard. Because of the accent on mamir├й, I have supplied тАШwhenтАЩ with the first half of p─Бda c, though the accent may simply result from the adjacency of the two verbs mamir├й and yem├║с╕е.

The verb in d, ant├бс╕е тАж dhuс╕е, is not a standard expression for тАШseparateтАЩ and in fact might be expected to mean тАШplace betweenтАЩ. Witzel Got┼Н tr. in that way, supplying тАЬLuftraumтАЭ (ant├бrikс╣гa-): тАЬZwischen die beiden тАж (Welten) setzten sie (den Luftraum) тАжтАЭ This is a clever solution and it may be the original sense of the lexeme, which, however, I believe has evolved to mean, without an object, тАШplace apartтАЩ, that is, separate by putting something in between.

I take dh─Б╠Бyase as belonging to тИЪdh─Б тАШsuckle, nourishтАЩ, like the rest of the occurrences of this -as-stem. Renou (EVP), K├╝mmel (395), and Witzel Got┼Н all follow this root assignment, but Geldner and Renou (Hymnes sp├йc.) take it to тИЪdh─Б тАШplaceтАЩ: тАЬdamit sie (die Herrschaft) aus├╝benтАЭ and тАЬpour quтАЩils se tiennent stables,тАЭ respectively. The separation of the two worlds is often presented as a boon for humans, so the тАШnourishтАЩ interpr. seems more fitting, and the usual analysis of dh─Б╠Бyas- supports it.

Griffith

Assuming in this world mysterious natures, they decked the heaven and earth for high dominion,
Measured with measures, fixed their broad expanses, set the great worlds apart held firm for safety.

Geldner

Und sie salbten beide Rodasi zur Herrschaft, indem sie hier ihre geheimen Spuren hinterlie├Яen. Sie haben die beiden in ihren Ma├Яen gleich gemacht und die Welten in Ordnung gehalten. Sie schieden die beiden Gro├Яen, die zusammengesto├Яen waren, damit sie die Herrschaft aus├╝ben.

Grassmann

Dort niederlegend das Geheimnissvolle, schm├╝ckten sie beide Welten zur Herrschaft aus, und massen sie mit Massen ab, dehnten sie weit aus, und stellten die beiden verbundenen geson- dert hin zur Labung.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey all ornamented (Indra) standing (in his car) and, clothed in beauty, he proceeds self-radiant; wonderful are the acts of that showerer (of benefits), the influencer (of consciences), who omniform, presides over the ambrosial (waters).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The influencer of consciences: the text has only asurasya; the term is explained by prerakasya antary─Бmitava, impeller, from being in the inner spirit

Jamison Brereton

As he was mounting they all tended to him. Donning beauties, he roams about with his own light.
Great is that name of the bull, the lord. Possessing all forms
[/Vi┼Ыvar┼лpa], he mounted the immortal (things/worlds).

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, I believe that this vs. turns to the first creation, before the poetsтАЩ intervention that was presented in vss. 2-3. It is appropriate that the entities described here are unidentified, for this is the time before the poets brought their verbal skills to bear. The central figure in this vs. is introduced merely by an acc. participle (─Бt├нс╣гс╣нhantam тАШmountingтАЩ). The form makes it clear that the referent is masculine and singular, but no other information is given; there is not even a pronoun. Likewise the subj. of the verb p├бri тАж abh┼лс╣гan тАШthey tendedтАЩ is given only as v├н┼Ыve тАШallтАЩ. Again we know the gender (masc.) and the number (pl.), but not the identity: poets (from vs. 2)? gods (the frequent default referent of v├н┼Ыve)? Rather than suggesting referents for these two entities as the standard tr. do, I think we should accept that the lack of referential clues is deliberate.

Certainly it continues through the verse, though some details accumulate. In b the тАШmountingтАЩ entity of p─Бda a is now presumably the subject. He wears beauties (┼Ыr├нyo v├бs─Бnaс╕е) and is self-luminous (sv├бrociс╕е); these descriptions begin to narrow the field, but not enough. (The only other occurrence of sv├бroci- modifies the Maruts, who are not likely to be in question here. And a number of different gods acquire ┼Ыr─л╠Б- .) In c he is identified as both a bull (or bullish one, vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan-) and a lord (├бsura-), neither particularly diagnostic, and the p─Бda claims to provide us with his тАЬgreat nameтАЭ (mah├бt тАж n─Б╠Бma). Indeed d seems at first to give us that name: vi┼Ыv├бr┼лpaс╕е.

But the joke is on us, for not only is vi┼Ыv├бr┼лpa- not a name but an epithet, but its literal meaning tells us that the lack of a single identifiable referent in this verse is the point. The word means тАЬhaving all forms,тАЭ and so the entity weтАЩve been chasing through the vs. is in fact protean and cannot be pinned down to a single identity.

He/it is creation before differentiation. (For a similar figure in a similarly mystical hymn in this maс╣Зс╕Нala, see III.56.3, where the androgynous figure is also called both a bull and vi┼Ыv├бr┼лpa.) The final p─Бda forms a tight ring with the first, in that the verb ─Б╠БтИЪsth─Б returns, and this time we get some indication of what he is mounting. But even this further specification falls short: it is simply amс╣Ы╠Бt─Бni, a neut. pl. adjective with multiple possible referents. This repetition makes the unfolding creation seem somewhat circular, but also incremental, in that new details accumulate, if slowly. But what seems to me an important clue has generally been ignored in the standard interpr. I find it impossible to believe that the repetition of ─Б╠БтИЪsth─Б was not deliberate, but all the standard tr. (save in part for Renou, Hymnes sp├йc, though he fell in line in EVP) render the two occurrences quite differently: the first literally (тАШmountтАЩ), but the second with the idiomatic meaning тАШassumeтАЩ, with Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н supplying тАШnamesтАЩ with the adj. тАШimmortalтАЩ (Geldner тАЬтАж hat er unsterbliche (Namen) angenommenтАЭ). There are two obvious things wrong with this interpr: 1) the lexeme ─Б╠БтИЪsth─Б is extremely common and I know of no passage where it means тАШassumeтАЩ; 2) translating it thus completely ignores the intra-vs. repetition, which at least to me is extraordinarily salient: the first word of the vs. is ─Б╠Бtiс╣гс╣нс╕еantam, the last tasthau. I therefore assume that the pf. in d also means тАШmountтАЩ and that the referent of the pl. тАШimmortalтАЩ is deliberately unspecified, but is something one could stand on – in this case probably тАШworldsтАЩ or some kind of solid тАШthingsтАЩ. Cf. VIII.52.7 (V─Бlakh.) ─Б╠Бtasth─Бv amс╣Ы╠Бtaс╣Г div├н тАЬ[it] has mounted to the immortal (world?) in heavenтАЭ and (with adh├н тИЪsth─Б) I.35.6 amс╣Ы╠Бt─Б╠Бdhi tasthuс╕е тАЬthey have taken their place on his immortal (foundations?).тАЭ The specification of a place to stand on enlarges the cosmic picture. Consider also 9c below with tasth├║с╣гo v├нr┼лp─Б тАЬof him surmounting the various forms,тАЭ with тИЪsth─Б and

-r┼лpa-.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe showerer (of benefits), the preceder and elder (of the gods), genitive rated (the waters); they are the abundant allayers of his thirst; sovereign Indra and Varuс╣Зa, grandsons of heaven, you possess the wealth (that is to be acquired) by the rites of the splendid sacrifice.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The earlier older bull gave birth. Here are his many proliferating riches. You two sons of heaven, with your insights you established your
dominion over the (cosmic) division, you kings, from olden days.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The unidentified creature in vs. 4, finally identified as a bull or as bullish (vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan- 4c), returns in this vs., with a slightly different тАШbullтАЩ designation (vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б-).

Here it is depicted as androgynous: though masc. in gender and called a bull, it gives birth (├бs┼лta). Androgyny is a powerful signal of the lack of differentiation I have been discussing, since perhaps the fundamental, universal binary contrast is male : female.

The bullтАЩs act of birth results in the desired differentiation that characterizes creation. This is expressed both by тАШmanyтАЩ (p┼лrv─л╠Бс╕е) in b and, indirectly, by the address to the two sons of heaven (d├нvo nap─Бt─Б) in cd. These two then seem to establish control over what has been created in the earliest time (prad├нvaс╕е тАШfrom olden daysтАЩ) and therefore implicitly preside over time.

I would now be inclined to interpr. p─Бda b as an expression of possession, тАЬHis are these many proliferating riches.тАЭ Cf. VI.3.3, also IV.23.8. However, the context is not definitive.

I interpr. and construe vid├бthasya in c differently from most, who take it with dh─лbh├нс╕е, with the interpr. further complicated by variant renderings of vid├бtha- (Geldner тАЬim Geiste der WeisheitтАЭ; Renou [EVP] тАЬgr├вce aux visions-po├йtiques de la c├йr├йmonieтАЭ; Witzel Got┼Н тАЬmit den Einsichten der (Beute-)VerteilungтАЭ). None of these makes a lot of sense to me, and therefore, despite the adjacency of vid├бthasya and dh─лbh├нс╕е, I construe the former instead with kс╣гatr├бm тАЬdominion of/over the (cosmic) division.тАЭ On this sense of vid├бtha- see comm. ad VIII.39.1: though the word generally refers to the ceremonial distribution of wealth and then to the ceremony where this happens, it can also refer to other types of division, including the parts of the cosmos. It may be somewhat more daring to assume that kс╣гatr├б- can take a genitive of what is ruled over – I do not now have parallels – but keep in mind that the root тИЪkс╣г─Б from which kс╣гatr├б- is derived regularly takes such a genitive. If my interpr. is correct, the vid├бtha- refers to the cosmic divisions produced by the 1st creation.

As noted in the published introduction, a number of referents have been suggested for the two sons of heaven, and as I also said there, I think this is missing the point. We remain in the realm of the 1st creation where entities may begin to proliferate but they are still not named. I suggested there that the two may be the two world halves (note that kс╣гatr├б- was associated with them in vs. 3b and see 8c below), but it is also quite possible that the focus should be on the тАЬtwo,тАЭ not on who exactly the two are: the first splitting of the primal unity.

Griffith

First the more ancient Bull engendered offspring; these are his many draughts that lent him vigour.
From days of old ye Kings, two Sons of Heaven, by hymns of sacrifice have won dominion.

Der ├дltere Bulle gebar als erster; diese seine Erfolge sind zahlreich. Ihr beiden Enkel des Himmels, ihr K├╢nige, ├╝bet im Geiste der Weisheit von jeher die Herrschaft aus.

Geboren ward der erste Held, der ├дltere [Varuna]; hier sind seine vielen St├дrkungen [kr├дftige Gaben], des Himmels beide S├╢hne [Mitra -Varuna] nahmen nach den Absichten der G├╢tter- gemeinde als K├╢nige von Alters her die Herrschaft ein."

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRoyal Indra and Varuс╣Зa, embellish the three universal sacrifices (and make them) full (of all requisites) for this celebration; you have gone to the rite, for I have beheld in my mind, at this solemnity, the gandharvas with hair (waving) in the wind.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The gandharvas: gandharv─Бn v─Бyuke┼Ы─Бn: the gandharvas are the guardians of the Soma, somarakс╣гak─Бn; similar beings are cited in Taittir─лya: sv─Бnabhr─Бj─Бn, bambh─Бre, hasta, suhasta, kс╣Ы┼Ы─Бс╣Зahete vaс╕е somakrayaс╣З─Бs, t─Бn rakс╣гadhvamm─Б vo dabhan

Jamison Brereton

O kings, you two tended to the three, to the many, to all the seats in the (cosmic) division.
Having come here with my mind, I saw even the wind-haired
Gandharvas under your commandment.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first half of vs. 6 simply expands on vs. 5. The same two kings have as their sphere of activity an increasing number (тАЬthree, many, allтАЭ tr─л╠Бс╣Зi тАж pur┼л╠Бс╣Зi тАж v├н┼Ыv─Бni) of тАЬseats,тАЭ that is (in my opinion), separated places, in the cosmic division (vid├бthe) also repeated from vs. 5. Note that the same verb p├бri тИЪbh┼лс╣г тАШtend toтАЩ returns from 4a, where тАШallтАЩ was the subject, not the object as here. In the 2nd hemistich the poet, who has been absent since vs. 2, returns, with his mind (m├бnas─Б), and sees the whole of creation in detail (or so I surmise), down to the wind-haired Gandharvas – all subject to the commandment of the two kings.

Griffith

Three seats ye Sovrans, in the Holy synod, many, yea, all, ye honour with your presence.
There saw I, going thither in the spirit, Gandharvas in their course with wind-blown tresses.

Geldner

Die drei, die vielen, alle Sitze schlie├Яest ihr beiden K├╢nige in eurer Weisheit ein. Ich sah, im Geiste dorthin gegangen, auch die Gandharven, deren Haare der Wind sind, in eurem Dienste.

Grassmann

ihr beiden K├╢nige, ihr schm├╝cktet aus die drei zahl- reichen G├╢ttergemeinden [vkl├дth├д zu lesen, vergleiche 492, 2; 659, 9, n├дmlich die drei im Himmel, in der Luft und auf der Erde] und alle ihre Sitze. Ich sah dort im Geiste hinwandernd die Gandharven mit windflatternden Haaren bei ihrem Werke.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд╕рднрд╛рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдореБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддреНрд░реАрдгрд┐) (рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдирд╛) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╢реБрднрдЧреБрдгреИрдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рдиреМ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдиреМ (рд╡рд┐рджрдереЗ) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдХреЗ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЗ (рдкреБрд░реВрдгрд┐) рдмрд╣реВрдирд┐ (рдкрд░рд┐) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐) рдЕрдЦрд┐рд▓рд╛рдирд┐ (рднреВрд╖рдердГ) рдЕрд▓рдВрдХреБрд░реБрдердГ (рд╕рджрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐) рд╕рднрд╛рдГ (рдЕрдкрд╢реНрдпрдореН) рдкрд╢реНрдпрд╛рдорд┐ (рдЕрддреНрд░) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд░рд╛рдЬрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЗ (рдордирд╕рд╛) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреЗрди (рдЬрдЧрдиреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН) рдЧрдиреНрддрд╛ (рд╡реНрд░рддреЗ) рд╕рддреНрдпрднрд╛рд╖рдгрд╛рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЗ (рдЧрдиреНрдзрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН) рдпреЗ рдЧрд╛рдВ рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдзрд░рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдиреН (рдЕрдкрд┐) (рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдХреЗрд╢рд╛рдиреН) рд╡рд╛рдпреБрд░рд┐рд╡ рдХреЗрд╢рд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рддрд╛рдиреН рееремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

тАЬThose who, for (the sake of) the showerer (of benefits), milk the agreeable (produce) of the cow, (who is known) by (many) names, they invested with the diversified strength (of the asuras) and practising delusive art have deposited their own nature in him.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This [=undifferentiated creation] was just hisтАФ(he who is both) bull (and) milk-cow; (then) with (individual) names they meted out the
тАЬfellowship of the cowтАЭ [=the joint creation of bull and milk-cow].

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. summarizes both creations. The first is dealt with glancingly in the first p─Бda. I take the neut. prn. t├бd тАШthisтАЩ as a reference to the not-yet-differentiated proto-creation, which belonged to and arose from the androgynous bovine of 5a, here explicitly identified first as masculine (asya: since this pronoun is unaccented, it does not modify what follows but functions as an autonomous pronoun), then as both bull (vс╣Ыс╣гabh├бsya, as in 5a) and milk-cow (dhen├│с╕е). This is the first appearance of any explicit feminine principle in this hymn.

The rest of the vs. concerns the second creation, with the original unitary t├бd divided and fitted out with names and forms. Note the return of the creation verb тИЪm─Б тАШmeasureтАЩ, with ─Б╠БтАж mamire (b) and n├н тАж mamire (d) echoing s├бm тАж mamire in 3c. The curious phrase s├бkmyaс╣Г g├│с╕е has caused some puzzlement among interpr.

Although by formation the hapax s├бkmya- appears to be a neut. abstract derived from тИЪsac тАШaccompanyтАЩ, the standard tr. (Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н) take the phrase as the equivalent of an animate creature, remarking that the companion of the cow must be the bull. But this not only ignores the abstract nature of s├бkmya- but also assumes that g├│с╕е here refers narrowly to a female bovine, though the stem is regularly used as a cover term for bovines of both sexes. I take the phrase as meaning тАЬthe fellowship of the cowтАЭ (or better, though more awkwardly, тАЬthe fellowship of the bovineтАЭ) as a poetic description of what was depicted in p─Бda a, the joint activity of the bull-and-cow and its product. This undifferentiated creation is then measured out into individual parts and equipped with names. The subject of ─Б╠БтАж mamire in b is not identified, but I assume it is the same m─Бy├нnaс╕е as the subject of n├н тАж mamire in d, whom I take to be the age-old poets we met in vss. 2-3.

Just as p─Бda b refers to the individual names, so does d refer to forms: the classical pairing of name-and-form (n─Бmar┼лpa) is thus distributed across the vs., as Geldner already pointed out (n. 7b). I take asmin here as referring to the creation (it), rather than to a putative тАШhimтАЩ (as most tr. do). In the course of their creative activity the poets assume various powers (p─Бda c) to enable their individualizing work.

Griffith

That same companionship of her, the Milch-cow, here with the strong Bull’s divers forms they stablished.
Enduing still some new celestial figure, the skilful workers shaped a form around him.

Geldner

Dies ist das Werk dessen, der Stier und Kuh ist. Sie haben den Gesellen der Kuh mit Namen ausgestattet. Indem sie immer andere asurische Gestalt anlegten, haben die Zauberkundigen ihre Gestalt ihm angepasst.

Sie [die Aditja’s] bildeten da nun dieses samenreichen Stieres [Agni] Eigenart durch die Wesenheiten des Rindes (?); in andre und andre G├╢ttergestalt sich kleidend, legten die weisen [Aditja’s] ihre Gestalt in ihn hinein.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬNo one (distinguishes) my golden lustre from that of this Savit─Б, in which (lustre) he has taken refuge; gratified by pious praise, he cherishes the all-fostering heaven and earth as a woman cherishes her offspring.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The Savit─Б: asya savitur nakir me: savit─Б = Indra, sarvasya jagato antary─Бmitay─Б prerayitur indrasya, of Indra the impeller, through his being the internal pervader of the whole world

Jamison Brereton

This [=creation] was just his, the impellerтАЩs, (it was) nothing of mineтАФ the golden emblem that he fixed firm.
But it is through (my) good praise hymn that the two world-halves set everything in motion here. He has swaddled the generations, like a
young woman her children.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As was indicated in the published introduction, this vs. is in certain ways a rephrasing of vs. 7, but updated, as it were, to the present day. The vs. begins exactly as vs. 7 did: t├бd ├нn nv ├аsya, followed by a genitive specifying the identity of the asya (vс╣Ыс╣г├бbhasya 7a, savit├║с╕е 8a), a signal that vs. 8 is a second version of the immediately preceding vs. Hence, by my interpr., savit├бr- is the equivalent of the original creator, the bull-cow of 5a and 7a. I therefore do not think that this refers to the god Savitar, but is rather to be taken in its literal sense as тАЬthe impeller.тАЭ Or rather, since b = VII.38.1b (a Savitar vs.), the poet is identifying Savitar in his most generic sense with the Ur-creator, the one who тАЬset in motion / impelledтАЭ the creation.

The poet disclaims any part in that original creation (n├бkir me), and the firmly fixed golden emblem of b seems to me to represent the static, undifferentiated result of the first creation. It reminds us of the hiraс╣Зyagarbha of X.121, another image of undifferentiated creation.

But in cd (at least in my view – the interpretations vary quite a lot) the poet identifies himself with the poets of old (of 7bcd). In c most tr. supply a verb, with the r├│das─л phrase as its object. I think, by contrast, that this is a nominal sentence with r├│das─л as subject. The two world-halves are credited with a role in the second creation, the same role they may play in 5cd (see comm. there): they set everything in motion. But they do so through the stimulus of a suс╣гtut├н-, a тАШgood praise-hymnтАЩ, and I take this praise-hymn to be the product of the 1st ps. poet, who disavowed a role in the first creation in 8a, but takes credit for contributing to the second creation in 8c.

The puzzling p─Бda to me is d, and my published translation is opaque even to me. I have now rethought it and will propose here a modified tr. and interpr. First, I suggest returning to GrassmannтАЩs grammatical analysis of vavre as a 1st sg., not a 3rd sg. (as all subsequent tr. have taken it, incl. my published translation). I take the p─Бda now as the current poetтАЩs boast, asserting his place in the poetic lineage. The lexeme ├бpi тИЪvс╣Ы means тАШswaddle, cover overтАЩ, as the simile of the woman and her children (one reading of j├бnim─Бni here) makes clear. But such a meaning can both be protective and somewhat arrogant or threatening. To understand the sense of the frame here, we need to go back to 2a, where the tremulous poet asked the previous generations (j├бnim─Б) of poets about their creative acts. I think these same poetic generations are whatтАЩs referred to here, but here our newly confident poet тАЬcoversтАЭ them – on the one hand, in a protective sense, like the young woman swaddling her children. He protects their legacy by continuing it. But тАШcover overтАЩ can also mean тАШconcealтАЩ, and in this sense the poet boasts that he will (or has?) become more skilled than they and cover up their achievements with his own. I would therefore retranslate the p─Бda as тАЬI have covered over / swaddled the (poetic) generations like a young woman her children.тАЭ

Griffith

Let no one here debar me from enjoying the golden light which Savitar diffuses.
He covers both all-fostering worlds with praises even as a woman cherishes her children.

Geldner

Dieses Werk von ihm, dem Savitri, kann mir keiner - wenn er sein goldenes Bildnis aufgerichtet hat. Mit sch├╢nem Loblied bringe ich die beiden alles hervorbringenden Rodasi her. Wie eine Frau ihre Kinder bedecken sie sch├╝tzend die Gesch├╢pfe.

Grassmann

Dies Wesen nun dieses Savitar niemand nennt es mir (?), den goldenen Schimmer, den er verbreitete; ganz h├╝llte er ein die hochgelobten alldurchdringenden Welten, wie die Mutter ihre Kinder.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou two secure the great felicity of the ancient (worshipper), that which is happiness in heaven; do you (therefore) be even about us; all those who exercise illusion, contemplate the manifold expoits of the everlasting and blandly-speaking Indra.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

All those who exercise illusion: vi┼Ыve m─Бyinaс╕е = sarve dev─Бс╕е, all the gods; m─Бy─Б also signifies wisdom, intelligence,hence, may also mean the wise;

M─Бya = deceivers, or asuras

Jamison Brereton

You two assure success to (that creation) of the age-old great one, (the creation) that is the divine blessing. May you two enfold us.
All masters of artifice look upon the deeds of him whose tongue is a herdsman, who surmounts the various forms.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As discussed in the published introduction, I take this vs. as showing both contributors to the second creation – the two (world-halves) from 8c and the masters of artifice (may├нnaс╕е) from 7d – bearing witness to our poetтАЩs new skill. In the first half of the verse the two (world-halves) begin by bringing to success the first creation of тАЬthe age-old great oneтАЭ (pratn├бsya тАж mah├бс╕е). I supply the equivalent of t├бd in p─Бda a, picked up by y├бd at the end of the p─Бda and further specified by da├нv─л svast├нс╕е beginning b. The standard tr. instead take a and b as separate clauses, with da├нv─л svast├нс╕е somewhat loosely construed with b.

In c the sequence gop─Б╠Бjihvasya is variously interpr. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н), Renou (Hymnes sp├йc.), and at least partially Oldenberg read it as two words, the first nom. gop─Б╠Б, the 2nd emended to j─лv├бsya (Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н) or jagatas (Renou; he gives no accent, but it should be j├бgatas) – attaching p─Бda c to b and taking d as a separate clause. I see no reason in this case to go against the Pp, which considers the form a cmpd, much less to emend the text so severely. Instead I take the two apparent genitives in c (gop─Б╠Бjihvasya tasth├║с╣гaс╕е) as referring to the current poet: he boasts that his tongue is a herdsman – that is, it marshals words – and that he surmounts the various forms (v├нr┼лp─Б) – that is, he has (verbal) control over the differentiated forms of the second creation. The poet has achieved his vocation. For the tongue, see vs. 3 of the following hymn (III.39.3b), where the poem, the hymnic vision, тАЬmounts the tip of (the poetтАЩs) tongue.тАЭ A form of the root тИЪsth─Б is also found in the same p─Бda.

Griffith

Fulfil, ye twain, his work, the Great, the Ancient: as heavenly blessing keep your guard around us.
All the wise Gods behold his varied actions who stands erect, whose voice is like a herdsman’s.

Geldner

Ihr beide f├╝hret das Werk des Gro├Яen, Uralten aus. Als g├╢ttliches Heil m├╢get ihr um uns sein, als die verschiedengestalteten H├╝ter des Lebendigen, des Unbeweglichen. Alle sehen die Werke des Zauberkundigen.

Grassmann

Lasset ihr beide [Mitra -Varuna] gelingen das Werk des uralten erhabenen [Agni], seid um uns als g├╢ttlicher Segen (?), alle weisen [G├╢tter] beschauen die vielgestaltigen Werke dessen [Agni], der aufrecht steht, und dessen Zunge beh├╝tet (?).

English translation:

тАЬWe invoke for our protection the opulent Indra, distinguished in this combat, the leader in the food-bestowing (strife), hearing (our praises), terrible in battles, the destroyer of foes, the conqueror of wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

тАУ For blessing we would invoke bounteous Indra, most manly, at this raid, at the winning of the prize of victory,
the strong one who listens, (we would invoke) for help in battles, him who smashes obstacles, the winner of prizes.

Griffith

Call we on Indra, Maghavan, auspicious, best Hero in the fight where spoil is gathered,
The Strong, who listens, who gives aid in battles, who slays the Vrtras, wins and gathers riches.

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрди рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдиреНрди рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░ рдХреЗ рд╕реБрдЦ рдФрд░ рджреБрдГрдЦ рдХреА рд╡рд╛рд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЛ рд╕реБрдирддреЗ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рддрд╛рдбрд╝рди рдХрд░рддреЗ рдФрд░ рд╕рддреНрдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░ рдХреЗ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рдХреА рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрдд рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдп рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рд╕реБрдЦреА рд╣реЛрд╡реИрдВ реерезрежрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкреА рд╕рднрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдФрд░ рднреВрдорд┐ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рейрео рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд реирек рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рдФрд░ рей рдордгреНрдбрд▓ рдореЗрдВ рей рдЕрдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рд╡рдпрдореВрддрдпреЗрд╜рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддреМ рднрд░реЗ рд╢реБрдирдВ рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдВ рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рдиреГрддрдордореБрдЧреНрд░рдВ рд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ рдШреНрдирдиреНрддрдВ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рджрджрддрдВ рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдЮреНрдЬрд┐рддрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рд╣реБрд╡реЗрдо рддрдереИрддрдВ рдпреВрдпрдордкреНрдпрд╛рд╣реНрд╡рдпрдд реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╢реБрдирдореН) рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдирд┐рддрдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдореН (рд╣реБрд╡реЗрдо) рдЧреГрд╣реНрдгреАрдпрд╛рдо (рдордШрд╡рд╛рдирдореН) рдмрд╣реБрдзрдирд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрдореН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдВ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдирдореН (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН) (рднрд░реЗ) рдкрд╛рд▓рдиреАрдпреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпреЗ (рдиреГрддрдордореН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрдирд╛рдпрдХрдореН (рд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕рд╛рддреМ) рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рд╕рддреНрдпрд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдЧреЗ (рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН) (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдореН) рдкрд╛рдкрдирд╛рд╢рд╛рдп рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡рд┐рдирдореН (рдКрддрдпреЗ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдп (рд╕рдорддреНрд╕реБ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ (рдШреНрдирдиреНрддрдореН) (рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐) рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ред рд╡реГрддреНрд░рдорд┐рддрд┐ рдзрдирдирд╛режред рдирд┐рдШрдВреж реиред резрежред (рд╕рдЮреНрдЬрд┐рддрдореН) рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧреНрдЬрдпрд╢реАрд▓рдВ рд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░рдореН (рдзрдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН) реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдирд╛рдГ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рдкреНрд░реАрддрд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдпреЛрд╜рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕реБрдЦрджреБрдГрдЦрд╡рд╛рд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рдГ рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреН рддрд╛рдбрдпрдиреНрддрдГ рд╕рддреНрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдиреН рд╕рддреНрдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреЛрд╜рдиреНрдпреЛрдиреНрдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕рддреНрдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕реЗрдпреБрд╕реНрддреЗ рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдВ рд▓рдмреНрдзреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрдЦрд┐рдирдГ рд╕реНрдпреБрд░рд┐рддрд┐ реерезрежрееред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдЪреНрдЫрд┐рд▓реНрдкрд┐рд╕рднрд╛рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрднреВрдореНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рейрео рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ реирек рд╡рд░реНрдЧрдГ рей рдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рей рдЕрдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд╡ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдиреНрди рдХрд░реВрди рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рд╛рдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реБрдЦ-рджреБрдГрдЦрд╛рдЪреА рд╡рд╛рд░реНрддрд╛ рдРрдХрддрд╛рдд. рджреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдВрдЪреЗ рддрд╛рдбрди рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рд╡ рд╕рддреНрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░реВрди рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛рдЪреА рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд. рддреЗ рдЕрддреНрдпрдВрдд рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░реВрди рд╕реБрдЦреА рд╣реЛрддрд╛рдд. рее резреж рее
